[S000176] (HQ0005; New York Society of Model Engineers)  This led to an invitation from the Lackawanna Railroad to move into their Passenger Terminal in Hoboken,NJ.

[S000177] (HQ0005; New York Society of Model Engineers)  They had the space for what would become the largest model railroad in the world at that time.

[S000178] (HQ0005; New York Society of Model Engineers)  The space?

[S000179] (HQ0005; New York Society of Model Engineers)  Only the ornate waiting room for the recently discontinued ferry boats to 23rd Street in New York City.

[S000180] (HQ0005; New York Society of Model Engineers)  Here the layout was built.

[S000181] (HQ0005; New York Society of Model Engineers)  It was based on the Lackawanna Railroad from Hoboken to Scranton, Pa.

[S000182] (HQ0005; New York Society of Model Engineers)  It was magnificent; from the scale model of the Hoboken Terminal to the soaring Delaware Water Gap.

[S000244] (HQ0007; James P. Comer) James P. Comer (born James Pierpont Comer, September 25, 1934 in East Chicago, Indiana) is currently the Maurice Falk Professor of Child Psychiatry at the Yale Child Study Center and has been since 1976.

[S000245] (HQ0007; James P. Comer)  He is also an associate dean at the Yale School of Medicine.

[S000246] (HQ0007; James P. Comer)  As one of the world's leading child psychiatrists, he is best known for his efforts to improve the scholastic performance of children from lower-income and minority backgrounds which led to the founding of the Comer School Development Program in 1968.

[S000247] (HQ0007; James P. Comer)  His program has been used in more than 600 schools in eighty-two school districts.

[S000248] (HQ0007; James P. Comer)  He is the author of ten books, including the autobiographical "Maggie’s American Dream: The Life and Times of a Black Family", 1988; "Leave No Child Behind: Preparing Today's Youth for Tomorrow's World", 2004; and his most recent book, "What I Learned in School: Reflections on Race, Child Development, and School Reform", 2009.

[S000249] (HQ0007; James P. Comer)  He has also written more than 150 articles for Parents (magazine) and more than 300 articles on children's health and development and race relations.

[S000250] (HQ0007; James P. Comer)  Dr. Comer has also served as a consultant to the Children's Television Workshop (Sesame Workshop) which produces Sesame Street and The Electric Company (1971 TV series).

[S000251] (HQ0007; James P. Comer)  He is a co-founder and past president of the Black Psychiatrists of America and has served on the board of several universities, foundations, and corporations.

[S000252] (HQ0007; James P. Comer)  He has also lectured and consulted widely not only across the United States at different universities, medical schools, and scientific associations, but also around the world in places such as London, Paris, Tokyo, Dakar, Senegal and Sydney, Australia.

[S000253] (HQ0007; James P. Comer)  For his work and scholarship, Dr. Comer has been awarded 47 honorary degrees and has been recognized by numerous organizations.

[S000410] (HQ0010; Mendocino County GMO Ban) Mendocino County, California, was the first jurisdiction in the United States to ban the cultivation, production or distribution of genetically modified organisms (GMOs).

[S000411] (HQ0010; Mendocino County GMO Ban)  The ordinance, entitled Measure H, was passed by referendum on March 2, 2004.

[S000412] (HQ0010; Mendocino County GMO Ban)  Initiated by the group "GMO Free Mendocino", the campaign was a highly publicized grassroots effort by local farmers and environmental groups who contend that the potential risks of GMOs to human health and the ecosystem have not yet been fully understood.

[S000413] (HQ0010; Mendocino County GMO Ban)  The measure was met with opposition by several interest groups representing the biotechnology industry, The California Plant Health Association (now the Western Plant Health Association) and CropLife America, a Washington-based consortium whose clients represent some of the largest food distributors in the nation, including Monsanto, DuPont and Dow Chemical.

[S000414] (HQ0010; Mendocino County GMO Ban)  Since the enactment of the ordinance, Mendocino County has been added to an international list of "GMO free zones."

[S000415] (HQ0010; Mendocino County GMO Ban)  Pre-emptive statutes banning local municipalities from such ordinances have now become widespread with adoption in sixteen states.

[S000416] (HQ0010; United States Senate election in Illinois, 1978) The 1978 United States Senate election in Illinois took place on November 7, 1978.

[S000417] (HQ0010; United States Senate election in Illinois, 1978)  Incumbent Republican United States Senator Charles H. Percy ran for re-election to a third term in the United States Senate.

[S000418] (HQ0010; United States Senate election in Illinois, 1978)  Percy was opposed by Democratic nominee Alex Seith, an attorney who had been appointed to several local government positions.

[S000419] (HQ0010; United States Senate election in Illinois, 1978)  Though Percy had been expected to coast to re-election over Seith, a first-time candidate, the election quickly became competitive.

[S000420] (HQ0010; United States Senate election in Illinois, 1978)  In the last few days of the campaign, a desperate Percy ran a television advertisement that featured him apologizing and acknowledging that, "I got your message and you're right."

[S000421] (HQ0010; United States Senate election in Illinois, 1978)  Percy's last-ditch effort appeared to have paid off, as he was able to edge out Seith to win what would end up being his third and final term in the Senate.

[S000458] (HQ0011; University of Missouri–Kansas City) The University of Missouri–Kansas City (UMKC) is a public research university serving the greater Kansas City metropolitan area.

[S000459] (HQ0011; University of Missouri–Kansas City)  Located in Kansas City, Missouri, UMKC is one of four system campuses that collectively constitute the University of Missouri.

[S000460] (HQ0011; University of Missouri–Kansas City)  UMKC is spread across multiple locales; the main Volker Campus, home to the majority of university operations, is located in Kansas City's Rockhill neighborhood, east of the Country Club Plaza, and adjacent to both the Stowers Institute for Medical Research and the world-renowned Linda Hall Library.

[S000461] (HQ0011; University of Missouri–Kansas City)  In 2017 the University, in collaboration with Truman Medical Center, Children's Mercy Hospital, the Missouri Health Department, the Jackson County Medical Examiners Office, and the Missouri Department of Mental Health Behavioral Medicine, formed the UMKC Health Sciences District on Hospital Hill.

[S000462] (HQ0011; University of Missouri–Kansas City)  This district is a first-in-the-nation partnership between local and state governments, the university, and these nationally recognized healthcare faculties, designed to promote collaboration in research, innovation, education, grant funding, and community outreach, for the advancement of health and wellness in the greater Kansas City metropolitan area.

[S000463] (HQ0011; University of Missouri–Kansas City)  Also in 2017, the university announced plans to expand its metropolitan identity with the construction of a downtown Campus for the Arts, located near the Kauffman Center for the Performing Arts.

[S000465] (HQ0011; Kansas City jazz) Kansas City jazz is a style of jazz that developed in Kansas City, Kansas and Kansas City, Missouri and the surrounding Kansas City Metropolitan Area during the 1930s and marked the transition from the structured big band style to the musical improvisation style of Bebop.

[S000466] (HQ0011; Kansas City jazz)  The hard-swinging, bluesy transition style is bracketed by Count Basie who in 1929 signed with the Bennie Moten's Kansas City Orchestra and Kansas City native Charlie Parker who was to usher in the Bebop style in the 1940s.

[S000467] (HQ0011; Kansas City jazz)  According to a Kansas City website, "While New Orleans was the birthplace of jazz, America's music grew up in Kansas City".

[S000468] (HQ0011; Kansas City jazz)  Kansas City is known as one of the most popular "cradles of jazz".

[S000469] (HQ0011; Kansas City jazz)  Other cities include New Orleans, Chicago, St. Louis, Pittsburgh, Philadelphia, and New York City.

[S000470] (HQ0011; Kansas City Scout) Kansas City Scout is one of the United States' largest electronic traffic management systems.

[S000471] (HQ0011; Kansas City Scout)  It was created in 2000 as part of a bi-state initiative between the Missouri Department of Transportation and the Kansas Department of Transportation to provide this system for the Kansas City Metropolitan Area, which is in both Missouri and Kansas (the anchor city of Kansas City is in Missouri).

[S000472] (HQ0011; Kansas City Scout)  The project's cost was $43 million.

[S000473] (HQ0011; Kansas City Scout)  Of that amount, the Federal Highway Administration (FHWA) contributed 80-90 percent of the project cost.

[S000474] (HQ0011; Kansas City Scout)  KDOT and MoDOT shared the remaining cost.

[S000475] (HQ0011; Kansas City Scout)  The system employs a system of electronic boards placed on major highways throughout the metropolitan area that display traffic information whenever information needs to be displayed (due to an accident, lane closure, highway closure etc.), and the system also has cameras on those billboards to automatically detect traffic problems.

[S000476] (HQ0011; Kansas City Scout)  While the system has extensive coverage of highways in the Kansas City Metropolitan Area it still has much more to cover.

[S000477] (HQ0011; Kansas City Scout)  Since it would be too expensive to cover all the major highways in the Kansas City metro (which has more miles of highway per person than any other metropolitan area in the United States), studies were conducted to determine which highways or segments of highways have priority due to higher accident rates.

[S000478] (HQ0011; Kansas City Scout)  Since the project's beginning, it has expanded greatly, and will continue to expand.

[S000479] (HQ0011; Kansas City Scout)  Future plans are to extend coverage to I-635 and cover I-435 even more (especially in the northern areas of the metro) as well as other major city highways.

[S000480] (HQ0011; Kansas City Scout)  It was named after the iconic Kansas City Scout Statue that exists in Penn Valley Park, overlooking Downtown Kansas City.

[S000484] (HQ0011; Downtown Kansas City)  However, the definition used by the Downtown Council is the most commonly accepted.

[S000485] (HQ0011; Kansas City metropolitan area) The Kansas City metropolitan area is a 15-county metropolitan area anchored by Kansas City, Missouri, that straddles the border between the U.S. states of Missouri and Kansas.

[S000486] (HQ0011; Kansas City metropolitan area)  With a population of about 2,340,000, it ranks as the second largest metropolitan area with its core in Missouri (after Greater St. Louis).

[S000487] (HQ0011; Kansas City metropolitan area)  Alongside Kansas City, the area includes a number of other cities and suburbs, the largest being Overland Park, Kansas; Kansas City, Kansas; Olathe, Kansas; and Independence, Missouri; each over 100,000 in population.

[S000491] (HQ0011; History of the Kansas City metropolitan area) The history of the Kansas City metropolitan area begins in the 19th century as Frenchmen from St. Louis, Missouri moved up the Missouri River to trap for furs and trade with the Native Americans.

[S000492] (HQ0011; History of the Kansas City metropolitan area)  The Kansas City metropolitan area, straddling the border between Missouri and Kansas at the confluence of the Kansas and Missouri Rivers, was a strategic point for commerce and security.

[S000493] (HQ0011; History of the Kansas City metropolitan area)  Kansas City, Missouri was founded in 1838 and defeated its rival Westport to become the predominant city west of St. Louis.

[S000494] (HQ0011; History of the Kansas City metropolitan area)  The area played a major role in the westward expansion of the United States.

[S000495] (HQ0011; History of the Kansas City metropolitan area)  The Santa Fe, and Oregon trails ran through the area.

[S000496] (HQ0011; History of the Kansas City metropolitan area)  In 1854, when Kansas was opened to Euro-American settlement, the Missouri-Kansas border became the first battlefield in the conflict in the American Civil War.

[S000497] (HQ0011; University of Kansas) The University of Kansas, often referred to as KU or Kansas, is a public research university in the U.S. state of Kansas.

[S000498] (HQ0011; University of Kansas)  The main campus in Lawrence, one of the largest college towns in Kansas, is on Mount Oread, the highest elevation in Lawrence.

[S000499] (HQ0011; University of Kansas)  Two branch campuses are in the Kansas City metropolitan area: the Edwards Campus in Overland Park, and the university's medical school and hospital in Kansas City.

[S000500] (HQ0011; University of Kansas)  There are also educational and research sites in Parsons, Topeka, Garden City, Hays, and Leavenworth, and branches of the medical school in Wichita and Salina.

[S000501] (HQ0011; University of Kansas)  The university is one of the 62 members of the Association of American Universities.

[S000553] (HQ0013; Hammerjack's)  The bands ranged from punk, glam, and heavy metal acts most commonly associated with the venue (e.g., Guns n Roses, Kix, Ratt, Skid Row or Extreme) to pop (e.g., Badfinger) and alternative rock groups (e.g., Goo Goo Dolls).

[S000613] (HQ0014; Real estate technology)  Besides for own stay, there are investors who generate income and capital gains by investing in different categories of Real Estate properties over time - They are broadly residential, commercial and industrial.

[S000614] (HQ0014; Real estate technology)  Historically used as a more tactical investment or for providing portfolio alpha, real estate has been used as part of a long-term core strategy due to increased market efficiency and increasing concerns about the future long-term variability of stock and bond returns.

[S000655] (HQ0015; 1996 FA Charity Shield)  The match was played on 11 August 1996 at Wembley Stadium and contested by Manchester United, who had won the Double of Premier League and FA Cup in 1995–96, and Newcastle United, who had finished as runners-up in the Premier League.

[S000664] (HQ0015; 1995–96 Manchester United F.C. season)  United finished the season by becoming the first English team to win the Double (league title and FA Cup) twice.

[S000665] (HQ0015; 1995–96 Manchester United F.C. season)  Their triumph was made all the more remarkable by the fact that Alex Ferguson had sold experienced players Paul Ince, Mark Hughes and Andrei Kanchelskis before the start of the season, and not made any major signings.

[S000677] (HQ0016; Fishing Lake) Fishing Lake is a lake in the Canadian province of Saskatchewan.

[S000678] (HQ0016; Fishing Lake)  The lake is located between highway 5 and highway 16, 22 km north of the town of Foam Lake, Saskatchewan, and 24 km east of the town of Wadena, Saskatchewan.

[S000679] (HQ0016; Fishing Lake)  The lake does not have an effective outlet channel, and so is prone to flooding.

[S000680] (HQ0016; Fishing Lake)  Record floods in 2007 resulted in a plan by the Government of Saskatchewan to lower the level of the lake by digging a drainage channel.

[S000681] (HQ0016; Fishing Lake)  The Fishing Lake First Nation opposed this plan, and instead flood control berms were constructed.

[S000683] (HQ0016; Osage State Fishing Lake)  It is a mile east of US 75.

[S000684] (HQ0016; Osage State Fishing Lake)  Scranton, Kansas, is to the lake's northwest and Overbrook, Kansas, is to the northeast.

[S000685] (HQ0016; Osage State Fishing Lake)  Osage Lake is a freshwater man-made lake, constructed in 1955.

[S000686] (HQ0016; Osage State Fishing Lake)  It has a surface area of 140 acres, The parkland in which the lake is contained has 366 acreas of land, mostly tall grass prairie with numerous wooded areas.

[S000687] (HQ0016; Osage State Fishing Lake)  The lake is owned by the State of Kansas.

[S000689] (HQ0016; Brown State Fishing Lake)  The lake is 62 acres (0.25 km²) in area and up to 13 feet (4 m) deep.

[S000690] (HQ0016; Brown State Fishing Lake)  The area was formerly known as Brown County State Park, and is 8 miles (13 km) east of Hiawatha, Kansas.

[S000691] (HQ0016; Neosho State Fishing Lake) Neosho State Fishing Lake, also known as Lake McKinley is located in the state of Kansas.

[S000692] (HQ0016; Neosho State Fishing Lake)  Located 5 mi north on highway 59 and 4 mi east on 40th Rd from the city of Parsons, Kansas, USA.

[S000693] (HQ0016; Neosho State Fishing Lake)  Construction of this lake was completed in 1927.

[S000694] (HQ0016; Neosho State Fishing Lake)  The lake covers 92 acre of water.

[S000695] (HQ0016; Neosho State Fishing Lake)  There are 124 public use acres surrounding the lake.

[S000696] (HQ0016; Neosho State Fishing Lake)  Fishing, camping, and picnicking are popular activities.

[S000697] (HQ0016; Neosho State Fishing Lake)  The park has a shelter house, fishing piers, picnic tables, barbecue grills, vault toilets and water hydrant.

[S000698] (HQ0016; Neosho State Fishing Lake)  Below Lake McKinley dam is a catch and release youth fishing pond for anglers age 15 and under when with an accompanying adult.

[S000699] (HQ0016; Neosho State Fishing Lake)  The lake is operated by the Kansas Department of Wildlife and Parks.

[S000702] (HQ0016; Narrow Hills Provincial Park)  These include the Gem Lakes, Lower Fishing Lake, Upper Fishing Lake and others.

[S000703] (HQ0016; Shawnee State Fishing Lake) Shawnee State Fishing Lake is approximately eight miles northwest of Topeka, Kansas, and is in northern Shawnee County, Kansas.

[S000704] (HQ0016; Shawnee State Fishing Lake)  This lake is sometimes confused with Lake Shawnee, on the east side of Topeka.

[S000705] (HQ0016; Shawnee State Fishing Lake)  It is a 135 acre surface area lake with a maximum depth of 25 ft .

[S000706] (HQ0016; Shawnee State Fishing Lake)  This is a manmade freshwater lake, which was constructed in the late 1960s.

[S000707] (HQ0016; Shawnee State Fishing Lake)  The lake is widest at the dam, which is at the south end of the lake.

[S000708] (HQ0016; Shawnee State Fishing Lake)  It can be reached by a number of roads.

[S000710] (HQ0016; Shawnee State Fishing Lake)  To the north is 94th Street and on the west side is Humphrey Road.

[S000711] (HQ0016; Higgins Lake, Michigan) Higgins Lake is a small unincorporated community along the southern and western shores of Higgins Lake, a recreational and fishing lake in Roscommon County, in the U.S. state of Michigan.

[S000712] (HQ0016; Higgins Lake, Michigan)  Higgins Lake is the name of the post office for the area, with ZIP code 48627.

[S000713] (HQ0016; Higgins Lake, Michigan)  This ZIP code includes several other small communities and locales along the shores of the lake, including (moving counter-clockwise around the lake) Hillcrest, Lyon Manor, Detroit Park, Cook Corner, Sharps Corner, Almeda Beach, Oak Grove, Ritz Corner, Pine Bluffs, and Cottage Grove.

[S000714] (HQ0016; Higgins Lake, Michigan)  Since all have Higgins Lake as a postal address, they are often all considered as part of the Higgins Lake community.

[S000715] (HQ0016; Higgins Lake, Michigan)  The lake is situated on the boundary between Lyon Township on the west and Gerrish Township on the east.

[S000716] (HQ0016; Higgins Lake, Michigan)  US 127 passes on the west side of the lake while I-75 and M-18 both pass a few miles to the east.

[S000717] (HQ0016; Higgins Lake, Michigan)  Houghton Lake is just a few miles to the south.

[S000718] (HQ0016; Higgins Lake) Higgins Lake is a large recreational and fishing lake in Roscommon County, in the U.S. state of Michigan.

[S000719] (HQ0016; Higgins Lake)  The 9,900 acre (40 km²) lake is known for its deep, clear waters and is the 10th largest in Michigan with a shoreline of 21 mi .

[S000720] (HQ0016; Higgins Lake)  It is named after Sylvester Higgins, the first chief of the topographical department of the Michigan Geological Survey.

[S000721] (HQ0016; Higgins Lake)  It has a maximum width of 4 mi and a length of 7 mi with a maximum depth of 135 ft .

[S000722] (HQ0016; Higgins Lake)  The mean depth is 44 ft and the lake contains almost 20 billion cubic feet (570 million m³) of water.

[S000723] (HQ0016; Higgins Lake)  Its retention time is about 12.5 years.

[S000724] (HQ0016; Higgins Lake)  The lake's watershed covers 19,000 acres (77 km²).

[S000725] (HQ0016; Higgins Lake)  The twin-lobed lake receives half of its water from submerged springs, six percent from incoming streams, and the remainder from direct rainfall and runoff.

[S000726] (HQ0016; Higgins Lake)  It drains into Marl Lake by the Cut River which runs into Houghton Lake and eventually to Lake Michigan.

[S000727] (HQ0016; Higgins Lake)  A mile north of the lake, water flows into the Lake Huron watershed.

[S000728] (HQ0016; Commanda Lake) Commanda Lake (or Lake Commanda) is a lake in central Ontario, Canada.

[S000729] (HQ0016; Commanda Lake)  Located on the border between Patterson Township and Pringle Township, in the Almaguin Highlands region of the District of Parry Sound, it is fed by Gee Creek, Commanda Creek and Beaudry Creek and is drained by the Restoule River.

[S000730] (HQ0016; Commanda Lake)  The Lake is shaped like the number "3", its middle spur is called Deep Bay.

[S000731] (HQ0016; Commanda Lake)  The lake is home to one permanent island, located off a point in its east.

[S000732] (HQ0016; Commanda Lake)  This is a mud bottom lake and its water is "tea coloured."

[S000733] (HQ0016; Commanda Lake)  On the north shore of the lake is the community of Restoule, but cottages line many of the shore lines.

[S000734] (HQ0016; Commanda Lake)  Lots of crown land also surrounds the lake shore making it a very peaceful lake for people of all ages to enjoy.

[S000735] (HQ0016; Commanda Lake)  This lake has one public boat launch towards the southern end of the lake accessible on Commanda Lake Road.

[S000736] (HQ0016; Commanda Lake)  The lake is located at an altitude of 222 m (729 ft) above sea level.

[S000737] (HQ0016; Commanda Lake)  The lake is home to the Northern pike, Walleye, Smallmouth bass and Largemouth bass species of fish.

[S000738] (HQ0016; Commanda Lake)  Ice gets thick in the winter making this lake an all year round fishing lake.

[S000785] (HQ0018; Bernhard Bötel) Bernhard Bötel (1883–1953) was a German operatic tenor and actor who had an active career in Germany and Austria during the first half of the 20th century.

[S000786] (HQ0018; Bernhard Bötel)  He made recordings for several record labels during the early years of the recording industry, including His Master's Voice, Odeon Records, Polydor Records, Tri-Ergon, and Vox Records.

[S000787] (HQ0018; Bernhard Bötel)  On the stage he sang a variety of roles in operas and operettas from leading parts to comprimario roles.

[S000788] (HQ0018; Bernhard Bötel)  His stage repertoire included Belmonte in Wolfgang Amadeus Mozart's "Die Entführung aus dem Serail", Chapelou in Adolphe Adam's "Le postillon de Lonjumeau", Count Almaviva in Gioachino Rossini's "The Barber of Seville", Daniel in Franz Lehár's "The Merry Widow", the Duke of Mantua in Giuseppe Verdi's "Rigoletto", Gabriel von Eisenstein in Johann Strauss II's "Die Fledermaus", Indigo in Strauss' "Indigo und die vierzig Räuber", Jeník in Bedřich Smetana's "The Bartered Bride", Paolino in Domenico Cimarosa's "Il matrimonio segreto", Pâris in Jacques Offenbach's "La belle Hélène", Pietro in Franz von Suppé's "Boccaccio", and Wilhelm Meister in Ambroise Thomas' "Mignon".

[S000789] (HQ0018; Giuseppe Verdi (film)) Giuseppe Verdi is a 1938 Italian biographical film directed by Carmine Gallone and starring Fosco Giachetti, Gaby Morlay and Germana Paolieri.

[S000790] (HQ0018; Giuseppe Verdi (film))  The film portrays the life of the composer Giuseppe Verdi (1813-1901).

[S000791] (HQ0018; Giuseppe Verdi (film))  The casting of Giachetti as Verdi was intended to emphasise the composer's patriotism, as he had recently played patriotic roles in films such as "The White Squadron".

[S000792] (HQ0018; Giuseppe Verdi (film))  The film was made at the Cinecittà Studios in Rome.

[S000793] (HQ0018; Giuseppe Verdi (film))  The film is also known by the alternative title The Life of Giuseppe Verdi.

[S000797] (HQ0018; Giuseppe Verdi) Giuseppe Fortunino Francesco Verdi (] ; 9 or 10 October 1813 – 27 January 1901) was an Italian opera composer.

[S000798] (HQ0018; Teatro Giuseppe Verdi) Teatro Giuseppe Verdi (the Giuseppe Verdi Theatre) is a small opera house located in a wing of the Rocca dei Marchesi Pallavicino on the Piazza Giuseppe Verdi in Busseto, Italy, a town closely associated with the life of the opera composer, Giuseppe Verdi.

[S000799] (HQ0018; Teatro Giuseppe Verdi)  From the 13th century, the “rocca” or “fortress” was the family’s palace; it is now the city hall after being acquired by the municipality in 1856.

[S000800] (HQ0018; Teatro Giuseppe Verdi)  The theatre opened on 15 August 1868 and seats 300.

[S000801] (HQ0018; Ambroise Thomas) Charles Louis Ambroise Thomas (5 August 1811 – 12 February 1896) was a French composer, best known for his operas "Mignon" (1866) and "Hamlet" (1868, after Shakespeare) and as Director of the Conservatoire de Paris from 1871 till his death.

[S000802] (HQ0018; Armand Castelmary) Armand Castelmary, real name Comte Armand de Castan, born Toulouse 16 August 1834, died New York City 10 February 1897, was a French operatic bass.

[S000803] (HQ0018; Armand Castelmary)  He created roles in three major premieres at the Paris Opera – Don Diego in "L'Africaine" by Meyerbeer (1865), the Monk in Verdi's "Don Carlos" (1867), and Horatio in Ambroise Thomas's "Hamlet" (1868).

[S000804] (HQ0018; Armand Castelmary)  Castelmary also appeared at opera houses in England and the United States, and died onstage at the Metropolitan Opera House, New York, during a performance of "Martha" by Friedrich von Flotow.

[S000805] (HQ0018; Ferdinando Provesi) Ferdinando Angelo Maria Provesi (1770 – 1833) was a native of Parma, Italy.

[S000806] (HQ0018; Ferdinando Provesi)  He was regarded as one of the greatest Italian opera composers of the era .

[S000807] (HQ0018; Ferdinando Provesi)  Provesi is best known as being an early tutor of Giuseppe Verdi when he was the "Maestro di cappella" (master of music) at the St. Bartolomeo cathedral in Busseto (the town very close to Le Roncole, the village where Verdi was born.)

[S000808] (HQ0018; Ferdinando Provesi)  Provesi was also director of the municipal music school and local Philharmonic Society.

[S000809] (HQ0018; Ferdinando Provesi)  He began teaching Verdi in 1824 when the future composer was 11 years old.

[S000810] (HQ0018; List of major opera composers) This list provides a guide to opera composers, as determined by their presence on a majority of compiled lists of significant opera composers.

[S000811] (HQ0018; List of major opera composers)  (See the "Lists Consulted" section for full details.)

[S000812] (HQ0018; List of major opera composers)  The composers run from Jacopo Peri, who wrote the first ever opera in late 16th century Italy, to John Adams, one of the leading figures in the contemporary operatic world.

[S000813] (HQ0018; List of major opera composers)  The brief accompanying notes offer an explanation as to why each composer has been considered major.

[S000814] (HQ0018; List of major opera composers)  Also included is a section about major women opera composers, compiled from the same lists.

[S000815] (HQ0018; List of major opera composers)  For an introduction to operatic history, see opera.

[S000816] (HQ0018; List of major opera composers)  The organisation of the list is by birthdate.

[S000818] (HQ0018; Verdi, the King of Melody)  It is based on adult life events of the composer Giuseppe Verdi.

[S000820] (HQ0019; United States Assistant Secretary of State) Assistant Secretary of State (A/S) is a title used for many executive positions in the United States Department of State, ranking below the Under Secretaries.

[S000821] (HQ0019; United States Assistant Secretary of State)  A set of six Assistant Secretaries reporting to the Under Secretary for Political Affairs manage diplomatic missions within their designated geographic regions, plus one Assistant Secretary dealing with international organizations.

[S000822] (HQ0019; United States Assistant Secretary of State)  Assistant Secretaries usually manage individual bureaus of the Department of State.

[S000823] (HQ0019; United States Assistant Secretary of State)  When the manager of a bureau or another agency holds a title other than Assistant Secretary, such as "Director," it can be said to be of "Assistant Secretary equivalent rank."

[S000824] (HQ0019; United States Assistant Secretary of State)  Assistant Secretaries typically have a set of deputies, referred to as Deputy Assistant Secretaries (DAS).

[S000826] (HQ0019; Douglas J. Bennet)  He was the fifteenth president of Wesleyan University, in Middletown, Connecticut, from 1995 to 2007.

[S000827] (HQ0019; Douglas J. Bennet)  Before that, he served as Assistant Secretary of State for International Organization Affairs in the Clinton Administration (1993–95) and Assistant Secretary of State for Legislative Affairs in the Carter administration (1977–79), was the President and CEO of National Public Radio (1983–93), and ran the U.S. Agency for International Development under President Carter (1979–81).

[S000828] (HQ0019; Richard Nixon) Richard Milhous Nixon (January 9, 1913 – April 22, 1994) was the 37th President of the United States from 1969 until 1974, when he resigned from office, the only U.S. president to do so.

[S000829] (HQ0019; Richard Nixon)  He had previously served as the 36th Vice President of the United States from 1953 to 1961, and prior to that as a U.S. Representative and also Senator from California.

[S000901] (HQ0021; 2009 Singapore Grand Prix)  It was also the second Formula One race to be held at night.

[S000903] (HQ0021; 2009 Singapore Grand Prix)  Toyota's Timo Glock finished second and 2008 race winner Fernando Alonso took third position, making this the only race of the season with neither a Brawn nor a Red Bull driver on the podium.

[S000904] (HQ0021; 2009 Singapore Grand Prix)  This was also the last race of 2009 for Glock, as he was injured during qualifying for the Japanese Grand Prix and was replaced by test driver Kamui Kobayashi.

[S000905] (HQ0021; 2009 Singapore Grand Prix)  Heikki Kovalainen scored his last ever World Championship points at this race.

[S000985] (HQ0023; Universal remote) A universal remote is a remote control that can be programmed to operate various brands of one or more types of consumer electronics devices.

[S000986] (HQ0023; Universal remote)  Low-end universal remotes can only control a set number of devices determined by their manufacturer, while mid- and high-end universal remotes allow the user to program in new control codes to the remote.

[S000987] (HQ0023; Universal remote)  Many remotes sold with various electronic include universal remote capabilities for other types of devices, which allow the remote to control other devices beyond the device it came with.

[S000988] (HQ0023; Universal remote)  For example, a VCR remote may be programmed to operate various brands of televisions.

[S000989] (HQ0023; Remote control) In electronics, a remote control is a component of an electronic device used to operate the device wirelessly from a distance.

[S000990] (HQ0023; Remote control)  For example, in consumer electronics, a remote control can be used to operate devices such as a television set, DVD player, or other home appliance, from a short distance.

[S000991] (HQ0023; Remote control)  A remote control is primarily a convenience feature for the user, and can allow operation of devices that are out of convenient reach for direct operation of controls.

[S000992] (HQ0023; Remote control)  In some cases, remote controls allow a person to operate a device that they otherwise would not be able to reach, as when a garage door opener is triggered from outside or when a Digital Light Processing projector that is mounted on a high ceiling is controlled by a person from the floor level.

[S000993] (HQ0023; Apple Remote) The Apple Remote is a remote control device released in or after October 2005 by Apple Inc. for use with a number of its products which use infrared capabilities.

[S000994] (HQ0023; Apple Remote)  The device was originally designed to interact with the Front Row media program on the iSight iMac G5 and is compatible with some later desktop and portable Macintosh computers.

[S000995] (HQ0023; Apple Remote)  The first three generations of Apple TV used the Apple Remote as their primary control mechanism.

[S000996] (HQ0023; Apple Remote)  It has now been replaced with the Siri Remote in the fourth generation.

[S000997] (HQ0023; Apple Remote)  Prior to the Apple Remote, Apple produced several nameless IR remotes for products such as the Macintosh TV, TV tuner expansion boards, and the PowerCD drive.

[S000998] (HQ0023; Siri Remote) The Siri Remote is a remote control device released in tandem with the 4th Generation Apple TV at an Apple Keynote Address by CEO Tim Cook on October 26, 2015 by Apple Inc. The Remote is designed specifically to work with the always-on Siri capable Apple TV.

[S000999] (HQ0023; Siri Remote)  The device is a successor of the original Apple Remote.

[S001000] (HQ0023; Siri Remote)  It is also compatible with the Apple TV 4K.

[S001001] (HQ0023; NetSupport Manager) NetSupport Manager is a Windows-centric cross-platform remote control software, allowing remote screen control and systems management from a Windows or Windows Mobile device of Windows, Mac, Linux, Solaris and Mobile devices.

[S001002] (HQ0023; NetSupport Manager)  It was first released for DOS only networks in 1989.

[S001003] (HQ0023; NetSupport Manager)  It supports thumbnail display of unlimited remote systems (since version 10), and allows navigation between remote systems in a manner similar to a KVM switch.

[S001004] (HQ0023; NetSupport Manager)  Functionality includes file transfers, chat, and hardware/software inventory including software updates. Fewer features are supported for Linux and Mac clients.

[S001005] (HQ0023; NetSupport Manager)  In 2012 NetSupport introduced new software versions allowing Remote Control from iOS and Android tablets and smartphones as well as a new Mac OS Control.

[S001006] (HQ0023; NetSupport Manager)  Version 12 was released in October 2013, which extended platform support to include ChromeOS clients.

[S001007] (HQ0023; NetSupport Manager)  Mobile Remote Control from iOS and Android was also extended with additional capabilities.

[S001008] (HQ0023; NetSupport Manager)  All versions of NetSupport Manager require the pre-installation of the software on both the local (Control) and remote (Client) computers/devices prior to use.

[S001009] (HQ0023; Front Row (software)) Front Row is a discontinued media center software application for Apple's Macintosh computers and Apple TV for navigating and viewing video, photos, podcasts, and music from a computer, optical disc, or the Internet through a 10-foot user interface (similar to Windows Media Center and Kodi).

[S001010] (HQ0023; Front Row (software))  The software relies on iTunes and iPhoto and is controlled by an Apple Remote or the keyboard function keys.

[S001011] (HQ0023; Front Row (software))  The first version was released October 2005, with two major revisions since.

[S001012] (HQ0023; Front Row (software))  Front Row was removed and discontinued in Mac OS X 10.7.

[S001013] (HQ0023; Apple Watch) Apple Watch (stylized as WATCH) is a line of smartwatches developed, designed, and marketed by Apple Inc. It incorporates fitness tracking and health-oriented capabilities with integration with iOS and other Apple products and services.

[S001014] (HQ0023; Apple Watch)  The original generation of the device was available in four variants: Apple Watch Sport, Apple Watch, Apple Watch Hermès, and Apple Watch Edition; each distinguished by different combinations of cases and first- or third-party interchangeable bands.

[S001015] (HQ0023; Apple Watch)  Apple Watch relies on a wirelessly connected iPhone to perform many of its default functions such as calling and texting.

[S001016] (HQ0023; Apple Watch)  It is compatible with the iPhone 5 or later models running iOS 8.2 or later, through the use of Wi-Fi or Bluetooth.

[S001017] (HQ0023; Apple Watch)  Announced by Apple CEO Tim Cook in September 2014, the device was released in April 24, 2015.

[S001018] (HQ0023; Apple Watch)  The Apple Watch quickly became the best-selling wearable device with the supply of 4.2 million smartwatches in the second quarter of the 2015 fiscal year.

[S001019] (HQ0023; Apple Watch)  The second generation of Apple Watch, released in September 2016, includes two tiers: Apple Watch Series 2 and Apple Watch Series 1, which includes the S1P chip, but is otherwise identical to the original.

[S001020] (HQ0023; Apple Watch)  The Series 3 was announced at a presentation at Apple Park on September 12, 2017 and was released on September 22, 2017.

[S001021] (HQ0023; MacScan) MacScan is an anti-malware utility for Apple's Mac OS X developed by SecureMac.

[S001022] (HQ0023; MacScan)  It is aimed at removing malware (including spyware, Trojan horses, keystroke loggers, and tracking cookies).

[S001023] (HQ0023; MacScan)  It was the first anti-spyware program released for Mac OS X.

[S001024] (HQ0023; MacScan)  In addition, the application scans for remote administration programs, like Apple Remote Desktop, allowing users to verify that such programs are installed only with their authorization.

[S001025] (HQ0023; Trainmaster Command Control) Trainmaster Command (TMCC) is Lionel's electronic control system for O scale 3-rail model trains and toy trains that mainly ran from 1994 to 2006.

[S001026] (HQ0023; Trainmaster Command Control)  Conceptually it is similar to Digital Command Control (DCC), the industry's open standard used by HO scale and other 2-rail DC trains.

[S001027] (HQ0023; Trainmaster Command Control)  It has one advantage over DCC, in that TMCC-equipped locomotives can run simultaneously with non-TMCC locomotives and Lionel Legacy engines as well as LionChief and LionChief Plus equipped locomotives.

[S001028] (HQ0023; Trainmaster Command Control)  The latter require a dedicated remote controller.

[S001029] (HQ0023; Trainmaster Command Control)  MTH Corporation's DCS controller can be configured to control TMCC locomotives, and all four systems (TMCC, Legacy, LionChief/LionChief+ and DCS) can be operated on the same track simultaneously.

[S001030] (HQ0023; Trainmaster Command Control)  Each simply requires a constant track voltage (18 volts).

[S001031] (HQ0023; Trainmaster Command Control)  TMCC/Legacy "broadcasts" it's signal to the antenna on the locomotives which listen for signals that first identify the particular locomotive by number and then it issues given commands as to speed, direction, sounds, lighting and other features.

[S001032] (HQ0023; Trainmaster Command Control)  DCS performs similar functions but transmits a carrier over the rails which are picked up through the locomotive's electrical pickup contacts.

[S001033] (HQ0023; Trainmaster Command Control)  While TMCC/Legacy and DCS remote controls relay operator commands to a device that transmits them to the train (Command Base or Track Interface Unit), LionChief/LionChief+ also issue remote control commands but the remote and locomotive are married and each locomotive requires a separate remote control.

[S001034] (HQ0023; Trainmaster Command Control)  This system requires no additional wiring as the control is directly "narrowcast" to the locomotive in the same way as a television remote control or garage door opener functions.

[S001035] (HQ0023; Trainmaster Command Control)  In 2017, Lionel released a universal remote for LionChief+ that will learn addresses for up to three locos at a time, simplifying the operation of multiple trains.

[S001036] (HQ0023; Apple Remote Desktop) Apple Remote Desktop (ARD) is a Macintosh application produced by Apple Inc., first released on March 14, 2002, that replaced a similar product called "Apple Network Assistant".

[S001037] (HQ0023; Apple Remote Desktop)  Aimed at computer administrators responsible for large numbers of computers and teachers who need to assist individuals or perform group demonstrations, Apple Remote Desktop allows users to remotely control or monitor other computers over a network.

[S001095] (HQ0025; Goštautai) Goštautai (Lithuanian plural form), masculine Goštautas and feminine form Goštautaitė ("Polish" original, after Kasper Niesiecki - Gastoldowie, later transformed into Gasztołdowie) were a Lithuanian noble family, one of the most influential magnate families during the 15th and early 16th centuries.

[S001096] (HQ0025; Goštautai)  Their only serious rivals were the Kęsgailos, and from the end of the 15th century the fast rising in power and influence Radziwiłł family clan.

[S001097] (HQ0025; Goštautai)  It appears from the Latin original spelling of their name Gastoldus which is a variation of "castaldius" that they had been close to the Grand Dukes and that their function was to oversee ducal demesne.

[S001098] (HQ0025; Goštautai)  Most power family gained during the reign of Casimir Jagiellon.

[S001099] (HQ0025; Goštautai)  The castaldius of Vytautas, Andrius Goštautas might have been a voivode of Vilnius and Kreva, and father of Jonas, appears to have been the precursor of the family growth.

[S001100] (HQ0025; Goštautai)  The majority of the family's possessions (lands) were in the western part of the Duchy and eastern ethnic Lithuania.

[S001101] (HQ0025; Goštautai)  After the death of the last scion of the family, Stanislovas Goštautas, the Polish King and Grand Duke of Lithuania Sigismund II Augustus inherited his possessions as a matter of right, per Grand Duchy of Lithuania law.

[S001106] (HQ0026; Death of Abdul Wali) Abdul Wali was an Afghan man who died in US custody on June 21, 2003 at the age of 28.

[S001107] (HQ0026; Death of Abdul Wali)  At the time of his death, he had been held for three days at the US base 10 miles south of Asadabad, in Kunar Province, Afghanistan, on suspicion of involvement in a rocket attack on the same base.

[S001108] (HQ0026; Death of Abdul Wali)  The cause of his death was at first reported to be a heart attack, but this came into question when three members of the U.S. 82nd Airborne Division came forward to testify that CIA contractor David Passaro assaulted Wali.

[S001109] (HQ0026; Death of Abdul Wali)  Passaro, a former U.S. Army Ranger, allegedly beat Wali for two consecutive nights, causing grievous injuries including a fractured pelvis.

[S001110] (HQ0026; Death of Abdul Wali)  Prosecutors would charge that Passaro ordered soldiers not to allow Wali to sleep, limited his access to food and water and subjected him to two consecutive nights of interrogation and beatings.

[S001111] (HQ0026; Death of Abdul Wali)  Among other injuries, Wali suffered a suspected fractured pelvis that would have made it impossible for him to urinate.

[S001112] (HQ0026; Death of Abdul Wali)  Witnesses testified that during one session Passaro, while wearing combat boots, kicked Wali in the groin hard enough to lift him off the ground, threw Wali to the ground, beat Wali on the arms and legs with a heavy Maglite flashlight, and that Passaro also vigorously thrust a flashlight into Wali's abdomen.

[S001113] (HQ0026; Death of Abdul Wali)  After the second night of beatings, Wali begged the soldiers to kill him and moaned a phrase that meant, "I'm dying."

[S001114] (HQ0026; Death of Abdul Wali)  Wali died on his fourth day in custody.

[S001115] (HQ0026; Death of Abdul Wali)  He repeatedly denied any involvement in the rocket attacks.

[S001177] (HQ0027; 2010–11 VCU Rams men's basketball team)  This was the highest ranking in VCU's history and the highest ranking of any team from the CAA.

[S001178] (HQ0027; 2010–11 VCU Rams men's basketball team)  The 2011 NCAA tournament run by VCU is regarded as one of the best Cinderella runs of all time.

[S001179] (HQ0027; 2010–11 VCU Rams men's basketball team)  To date, they are the only men's Division I basketball team whose NCAA tournament journey ran from The First Four to the Final Four.

[S001180] (HQ0027; 2010–11 VCU Rams men's basketball team)  They are also the only team in the tournament to win five games, and not qualify for the national championship game.

[S001199] (HQ0028; Dictyosperma) Dictyosperma is a monotypic genus of flowering plant in the palm family found in the Mascarene Islands in the Indian Ocean (Mauritius, Réunion and Rodrigues).

[S001200] (HQ0028; Dictyosperma)  The sole species, Dictyosperma album, is widely cultivated in the tropics but has been farmed to near extinction in its native habitat.

[S001201] (HQ0028; Dictyosperma)  It is commonly called princess palm or hurricane palm, the latter owing to its ability to withstand strong winds by easily shedding leaves.

[S001202] (HQ0028; Dictyosperma)  It is closely related to, and resembles, palms in the "Archontophoenix" genus.

[S001203] (HQ0028; Dictyosperma)  The genus is named from two Greek words meaning "net" and "seed" and the epithet is Latin for "white", the common color of the crownshaft at the top of the trunk.

[S001204] (HQ0028; Huernia) The genus Huernia (family Apocynaceae, subfamily Asclepiadoideae) consists of stem succulents from Eastern and Southern Africa, first described as a genus in 1810.

[S001205] (HQ0028; Huernia)  The flowers are five-lobed, usually somewhat more funnel- or bell-shaped than in the closely related genus "Stapelia", and often striped vividly in contrasting colours or tones, some glossy, others matt and wrinkled depending on the species concerned.

[S001206] (HQ0028; Huernia)  To pollinate, the flowers attract flies by emitting a scent similar to that of carrion.

[S001207] (HQ0028; Huernia)  The genus is considered close to the genera "Stapelia" and "Hoodia".

[S001208] (HQ0028; Huernia)  The name is in honour of Justin Heurnius (1587–1652) a Dutch missionary who is reputed to have been the first collector of South African Cape plants.

[S001209] (HQ0028; Huernia)  His name was actually mis-spelt by the collector.

[S001210] (HQ0029; Edgar Kaiser Jr.) Edgar Fosburgh Kaiser Jr. (July 5, 1942 – January 11, 2012) was an American-Canadian financier and a former owner of the Denver Broncos American football team.

[S001211] (HQ0029; Edgar Kaiser Jr.)  He was born in Portland, Oregon on July 5, 1942 and is the grandson of shipbuilding industrialist Henry J. Kaiser.

[S001212] (HQ0029; Edgar Kaiser Jr.)  He earned a BA degree from Stanford University and an MBA degree from Harvard University.

[S001213] (HQ0029; Edgar Kaiser Jr.)  Kaiser served as a White House Fellow and as a Special Assistant to President Lyndon B. Johnson, President Richard M. Nixon, and as a Special Assistant to U.S. Secretary of the Interior Walter J. Hickel.

[S001214] (HQ0029; Edgar Kaiser Jr.)  He became a Canadian citizen in 1980.

[S001215] (HQ0029; Edgar Kaiser Jr.)  He died on January 11, 2012.

[S001217] (HQ0029; Eagle Mountain Railroad) The Eagle Mountain Railroad (EMRR) was a private railroad in California, owned by the Kaiser Steel Corporation, and is owned today by Kaiser Steel's successor, Kaiser Ventures, Inc. of Ontario, California.

[S001218] (HQ0029; Neafie &amp; Levy) Neafie, Levy & Co., commonly known as Neafie & Levy, was a Philadelphia shipbuilding and engineering firm that existed from the middle of the 19th to the beginning of the 20th century.

[S001219] (HQ0029; Neafie &amp; Levy)  Described as America's "first specialist marine engineers", Neafie & Levy was probably the first company in the United States to combine the building of iron ships with the manufacture of steam engines to power them.

[S001220] (HQ0029; Neafie &amp; Levy)  The company was also the largest supplier of screw propellers to other North American shipbuilding firms in its early years, and at its peak in the early 1870s was Philadelphia's busiest and most heavily capitalized shipbuilder.

[S001221] (HQ0029; Kaiser Shipyards) The Kaiser Shipyards were seven major shipbuilding yards located on the United States west coast during World War II.

[S001222] (HQ0029; Kaiser Shipyards)  Kaiser ranked 20th among U.S. corporations in the value of wartime production contracts.

[S001223] (HQ0029; Kaiser Shipyards)  The shipyards were owned by the Kaiser Shipbuilding Company, a creation of American industrialist Henry J. Kaiser, (1882-1967), who established the shipbuilding company around 1939 in order to help meet the construction goals set by the United States Maritime Commission for merchant shipping.

[S001224] (HQ0029; Kaiser Ventures) Kaiser Ventures (formerly Kaiser Steel) corporation, headquartered in Ontario, California.

[S001225] (HQ0029; Kaiser Ventures)  It was founded by Henry J. Kaiser to provide steel plate for the Pacific Coast shipbuilding industry, which expanded during World War II, then shrank, then expanded again during the Korean War.

[S001226] (HQ0029; Kaiser Ventures)  California Shipbuilding Corporation on Terminal Island, California, was one of these shipyards which built hundreds of Liberty ships and Victory ships in World War II, and was also a project of Henry Kaiser.

[S001227] (HQ0029; Kaiser Ventures)  Kaiser Steel was noted for making the most of its costly steelmaking inputs, and it captured, along with the U.S. Steel plant in Utah, much of the Pacific Coast steel market by the late 1950s.

[S001228] (HQ0029; Kaiser Ventures)  Its assets included steelmaking plants in Napa, California (that it acquired from Basalt Rock Company in 1955) and Fontana, California (now operated by California Steel Industries), and a former open-pit iron ore mine at Eagle Mountain, California.

[S001229] (HQ0029; Kaiser Ventures)  Steel manufactured was also used in Kaiser Motors.

[S001230] (HQ0029; Henry J. Kaiser) Henry John Kaiser (May 9, 1882 – August 24, 1967) was an American industrialist who became known as the father of modern American shipbuilding.

[S001231] (HQ0029; Henry J. Kaiser)  He established the Kaiser Shipyards, which built Liberty ships during World War II, after which he formed Kaiser Aluminum and Kaiser Steel.

[S001232] (HQ0029; Henry J. Kaiser)  Kaiser organized Kaiser Permanente health care for his workers and their families.

[S001233] (HQ0029; Henry J. Kaiser)  He led Kaiser-Frazer followed by Kaiser Motors, automobile companies known for the safety of their designs.

[S001234] (HQ0029; Henry J. Kaiser)  Kaiser was involved in large construction projects such as civic centers and dams, and invested in real estate.

[S001235] (HQ0029; Henry J. Kaiser)  With his wealth, he established the Kaiser Family Foundation, a nonprofit, non-partisan, charitable organization.

[S001236] (HQ0029; John Roach &amp; Sons) John Roach & Sons was a major 19th-century American shipbuilding and manufacturing firm founded in 1864 by Irish-American immigrant John Roach.

[S001237] (HQ0029; John Roach &amp; Sons)  Between 1871 and 1885, the company was the largest shipbuilding firm in the United States, building more iron ships than its next two major competitors combined.

[S001238] (HQ0029; John Roach &amp; Sons)  It was also by far the largest contractor to the U.S. Navy during this period, and at its peak is said to have been the nation's largest employer behind the railroads.

[S001239] (HQ0029; New York Shipbuilding Corporation) The New York Shipbuilding Corporation (or New York Ship for short) was an American shipbuilding company that operated from 1899 to 1968, ultimately completing more than 500 vessels for the U.S. Navy, the United States Merchant Marine, the United States Coast Guard, and other maritime concerns.

[S001240] (HQ0029; New York Shipbuilding Corporation)  At its peak during World War II, NYSB was the largest and most productive shipyard in the world.

[S001248] (HQ0030; St. Andre's Parish)  The parish was founded in 1860 to serve the city's large French-Canadian and French-American communities.

[S001250] (HQ0030; St. Andre's Parish)  Of those 8 Churches, only Saint Joseph, Most Holy Trinity, Saint Margaret, and Saint Philip remain open.

[S001251] (HQ0030; St. Andre's Parish)  (St. Brendan's has always, and continues to serve as a summer chapel.)

[S001256] (HQ0030; Mercenaries, Spies and Private Eyes) Mercenaries, Spies and Private Eyes ("MSPE") is a tabletop role-playing game designed and written by Michael A. Stackpole and first published in April 1983 by Blade, a division of Flying Buffalo, Inc.

[S001257] (HQ0030; Mercenaries, Spies and Private Eyes)  A second edition was later published by Sleuth Publications, but Flying Buffalo continues to distribute the game.

[S001258] (HQ0030; Mercenaries, Spies and Private Eyes)  "MSPE"'s mechanics are based on those of "Tunnels and Trolls", with the addition of a skill system for characters.

[S001262] (HQ0030; Crank Caverns) Crank Caverns is the common name of the remains of the Rainford Delph Quarry near Crank in St. Helens, Merseyside.

[S001263] (HQ0030; Crank Caverns)  It is a network of underground tunnels and caverns, as well as an extensive woodland.

[S001264] (HQ0030; Crank Caverns)  Information in the St. Helens local history archives states that sandstone quarrying began here as early as 1730.

[S001265] (HQ0030; Crank Caverns)  As the quarry expanded, the cost of purchasing land to open cast mine it increased, so it was decided to opt for a different method.

[S001266] (HQ0030; Crank Caverns)  Instead of quarrying out the stone, they would mine it out, following a seam of stone until it ran out.

[S001267] (HQ0030; Crank Caverns)  This resulted in the network of caves, tunnels and shafts we see today.

[S001268] (HQ0030; Crank Caverns)  Rainford Delph is listed as a Colliery by 1854, under the ownership of Charles Howarth or Yorkshire Charlie as he was known locally by 1880.

[S001269] (HQ0030; Crank Caverns)  Mining finally ceased and the woods and caverns were used as a game reserve by the Earl of Derby until 1939, when they became a storage facility for ammunition for the anti-aircraft position at Crank.

[S001270] (HQ0030; Crank Caverns)  After the war, the caverns ceased use as a game reserve.

[S001271] (HQ0030; Crank Caverns)  Today, Crank Caverns are not officially open to the public and due to their increasing instability, attempts have been made to close access to the caverns and tunnels themselves.

[S001272] (HQ0030; Crank Caverns)  Despite this, the site is still physically accessible from a nearby public footpath and is still a draw for generations of curious locals who wish to explore, many having heard the numerous local myths and legends from an early age.

[S001340] (HQ0032; Hailstorm Alley)  These storms frequently produce hail that is damaging to property.

[S001341] (HQ0032; Hailstorm Alley)  This area stretches from High River in southern Alberta, northward through Calgary, through Red Deer to Lacombe and then westward to Rocky Mountain House.

[S001342] (HQ0032; Hailstorm Alley)  It is known to be one of the worst areas in the world for damaging hail produced by thunderstorms.

[S001343] (HQ0032; Hailstorm Alley)  These are regarded as loose boundaries.

[S001344] (HQ0032; Hailstorm Alley)  While this area is common for damaging hailstorms, the reality is damaging hailstorms occur over much of central and southern Alberta every summer.

[S001345] (HQ0032; Hailstorm Alley)  The City of Calgary is regarded as the hailstorm capital of Canada.

[S001346] (HQ0032; Dewey Beard) Dewey Beard or Wasú Máza ("Iron Hail", 1858–1955) was a Minneconjou Lakota who fought in the Battle of Little Bighorn as a teenager.

[S001347] (HQ0032; Dewey Beard)  After George Armstrong Custer's defeat, Wasu Maza followed Sitting Bull into exile in Canada and then back to South Dakota where he lived on the Cheyenne River Indian Reservation.

[S001348] (HQ0032; Dewey Beard)  Chief Iron Hail is often mistaken by historians for Chief Iron Tail, being Lakota contemporaries with similar-sounding names.

[S001349] (HQ0032; Dewey Beard)  Most biographies incorrectly report that Chief Iron Tail fought in the Battle of the Little Bighorn and that his family was killed in 1890 at Wounded Knee, when in truth it was Chief Iron Hail who suffered the loss.

[S001370] (HQ0033; L'Oiseau bleu (Metzinger)) L'Oiseau bleu (also known as The Blue Bird and Der Blaue Vogel) is a large oil painting created in 1912–1913 by the French artist and theorist Jean Metzinger (1883–1956); considered by Guillaume Apollinaire and André Salmon as a founder of Cubism, along with Georges Braque and Pablo Picasso.

[S001371] (HQ0033; L'Oiseau bleu (Metzinger))  "L'Oiseau bleu", one of Metzinger's most recognizable and frequently referenced works, was first exhibited in Paris at the Salon des Indépendants in the spring of 1913 (n. 2087), several months after the publication of the first (and only) Cubist manifesto, "Du «Cubisme»", written by Jean Metzinger and Albert Gleizes (1912).

[S001372] (HQ0033; L'Oiseau bleu (Metzinger))  It was subsequently exhibited at the 1913 in Berlin (titled "Der blaue Vogel", n. 287).

[S001373] (HQ0033; L'Oiseau bleu (Metzinger))  Apollinaire described "L'Oiseau bleu" as a 'very brilliant painting' and 'his most important work to date'.

[S001374] (HQ0033; L'Oiseau bleu (Metzinger))  "L'Oiseau bleu", acquired by the City of Paris in 1937, forms part of the permanent collection at the Musée d'Art Moderne de la Ville de Paris.

[S001375] (HQ0033; Levasseur PL.8) The Levasseur PL.8 was a single engine, two-seat long-distance record-breaking biplane aircraft modified from an existing Levasseur PL.4 carrier-based reconnaissance aircraft produced in France in the 1920s.

[S001376] (HQ0033; Levasseur PL.8)  Levasseur built the aircraft in 1927, specifically for pilots Charles Nungesser and François Coli for a transatlantic attempt to win the Orteig Prize.

[S001377] (HQ0033; Levasseur PL.8)  Only two examples of the type were built, with the first PL.8-01 named "L'Oiseau Blanc" (The White Bird), that gained fame as Nungesser and Coli's aircraft.

[S001378] (HQ0033; Paul Sauvage (aviator)) Sergent Paul Joannes Sauvage was a French World War I flying ace credited with eight confirmed and six unconfirmed aerial victories.

[S001379] (HQ0033; Paul Sauvage (aviator))  He was originally posted to fly a Nieuport for Escadrille 65, and scored his first victory with them on 16 July 1916.

[S001380] (HQ0033; Paul Sauvage (aviator))  He became the youngest French ace on 2 October, and held that distinction until his death by anti-aircraft fire on January 7, 1917.

[S001381] (HQ0033; Wooster and Davis) Wooster and Davis-- Lieutenant Stanton Hall Wooster (April 1, 1895 Connecticut - April 26, 1927) and Lieutenant Commander Noel Guy Davis (December 25, 1891 Salt Lake City, Utah - April 26, 1927) were two United States Navy (USN) airmen who made an attempt to fly the Atlantic Ocean from New York-to-Paris in the spring of 1927.

[S001382] (HQ0033; Wooster and Davis)  The men were trying to win the $25,000 dollar Orteig Prize offered by New York hotelier Raymond Orteig for the first nonstop flight between New York and Paris.

[S001383] (HQ0033; Wooster and Davis)  Competitors for the prize were French World War One ace Rene Fonck and his crew of three, USN Commander Richard Evelyn Byrd, Clarence Chamberlain and a young airmail pilot named Charles Lindbergh.

[S001384] (HQ0033; Wooster and Davis)  On the Paris side of the Atlantic their competitors were another World War One French ace, Charles Nungesser, and his navigator Francois Coli.

[S001385] (HQ0033; L'Oiseau Blanc) L'Oiseau Blanc (commonly known in the English-speaking world as The White Bird ) was a French Levasseur PL.8 biplane that disappeared in 1927, during an attempt to make the first non-stop transatlantic flight between Paris and New York City to compete for the Orteig Prize.

[S001386] (HQ0033; L'Oiseau Blanc)  The aircraft was flown by French World War I aviation heroes, Charles Nungesser and François Coli.

[S001387] (HQ0033; L'Oiseau Blanc)  The aircraft took off from Paris on 8 May 1927 and was last seen over Ireland.

[S001388] (HQ0033; L'Oiseau Blanc)  Less than two weeks later, Charles Lindbergh successfully made the New York–Paris journey and claimed the prize, flying the "Spirit of St. Louis".
