[S002027] (HQ0047; Led Zeppelin Boxed Set 2)  This box set features the rest of the English rock band Led Zeppelin's catalogue not included in the 1990 4-CD box set "Led Zeppelin", all digitally remastered, including the previously unreleased studio track "Baby Come On Home".

[S002028] (HQ0047; Led Zeppelin Boxed Set 2)  A 54-page booklet was also included with the release.

[S002029] (HQ0047; Led Zeppelin Boxed Set 2)  Between this box set and the 4-CD box set every track from the band's nine studio albums are featured along with two BBC live recordings; the band's only non-LP b-side; and one studio outtake.

[S002030] (HQ0047; To Know Him Is to Love Him) "To Know Him Is to Love Him" is a song written by Phil Spector, inspired by words on his father's tombstone, "To Know Him Was To Love Him."

[S002031] (HQ0047; To Know Him Is to Love Him)  It was first recorded by the only vocal group of which he was a member, the Teddy Bears.

[S002032] (HQ0047; To Know Him Is to Love Him)  Their recording spent three weeks at No. 1 on the "Billboard" Hot 100 singles chart in 1958, while reaching No. 2 on UK's "New Musical Express" chart.

[S002033] (HQ0047; To Know Him Is to Love Him)  Peter & Gordon and Bobby Vinton later had hits with the song, with its title and lyrics changed to "To Know You Is to Love You".

[S002034] (HQ0047; To Know Him Is to Love Him)  In 1987, the song was resurrected by Dolly Parton, Linda Ronstadt and Emmylou Harris, whose "Trio" recording topped the U.S. country singles charts.

[S002035] (HQ0047; To Know Him Is to Love Him)  The song is in 12/8 time.

[S002036] (HQ0047; The Doors: Vinyl Box Set) The Doors: Vinyl Box Set is the seventh box set for the rock band The Doors.

[S002037] (HQ0047; The Doors: Vinyl Box Set)  It is a 7 record set of the original 6 Doors albums, remastered in stereo from the original analogue tapes with a mono version of the debut album.

[S002038] (HQ0047; The Doors: Vinyl Box Set)  Artwork, packaging, and inner sleeves are replicas of the originals from 1967-1971.

[S002039] (HQ0047; The Doors: Vinyl Box Set)  The box set was originally planned to be released in October 2007, but was delayed due to a problem with the vinyl, as well as other problems in the production of the box set.

[S002040] (HQ0047; The Doors: Vinyl Box Set)  The delay ran until February 2008.

[S002041] (HQ0047; The Doors: Vinyl Box Set)  Reasons for the delay included faulty test pressings, inferiority of the L.A. Woman artwork, and bad compounds in the vinyl that was used first, which caused a search for a new source of virgin vinyl.

[S002042] (HQ0048; Nikolai Podgorny) Nikolai Viktorovich Podgorny (Russian: Никола́й Ви́кторович Подго́рный ; ] , Ukrainian: Микола Вікторович Підгорний ; 18 February [O.S. 5 February] 1903 – 11 January 1983) was a Soviet statesman during the Cold War.

[S002043] (HQ0048; Nikolai Podgorny)  He served as First Secretary of the Central Committee of the Communist Party of Ukraine from 1957 to 1963 and as Chairman of the Presidium of the Supreme Soviet from 1965 to 1977.

[S002044] (HQ0048; Nikolai Podgorny)  He was replaced as Chairman of the Presidium of the Supreme Soviet in 1977 by General Secretary Leonid Brezhnev.

[S002045] (HQ0048; Nikolai Podgorny)  That same year he lost his seat in the Political Bureau (Politburo) and was forced to resign from active politics.

[S002046] (HQ0048; Andrei Kirilenko (politician)) Andrei Pavlovich Kirilenko (Russian: Андре́й Па́влович Кириле́нко ; ] ; 8 September [O.S. 26 August] 1906 – 12 May 1990) was a Soviet statesman from the start to the end of the Cold War.

[S002047] (HQ0048; Andrei Kirilenko (politician))  In 1906, Kirilenko was born at Alexeyevka in Belgorod Oblast to a Ukrainian working-class family.

[S002048] (HQ0048; Andrei Kirilenko (politician))  He graduated in the 1920s from a local vocational school, and again in the mid-to-late 1930s from the Rybinsk Aviation Technology Institute.

[S002049] (HQ0048; Andrei Kirilenko (politician))  He became a member of the All-Union Communist Party (bolsheviks) in 1930.

[S002050] (HQ0048; Andrei Kirilenko (politician))  As many like him, Kirilenko climbed up the Soviet hierarchy through the "industrial ladder"; by the 1960s, he was Vice-Chairman of the Bureau of the Central Committee of the Russian Soviet Federative Socialist Republic (RSFSR).

[S002051] (HQ0048; Andrei Kirilenko (politician))  After Nikita Khrushchev's forced resignation, Kirilenko became Leonid Brezhnev's "chief lieutenant" within the Central Committee.

[S002052] (HQ0048; MS Excelsior Neptune) MS "Excelsior Neptune" (originally, the "Feliks Dzerzhinskiy") was an ocean liner owned by the Soviet Union's Black Sea Shipping Company.

[S002053] (HQ0048; MS Excelsior Neptune)  She was built in 1958 by VEB Mathias-Thesen Werft, Wismar, East Germany, as one of the Mikhail Kalinin series of ships.

[S002054] (HQ0048; MS Excelsior Neptune)  It was named after Felix Dzerzhinsky, a Soviet statesman and founder of the Soviet secret police (Cheka).

[S002055] (HQ0048; Mikhail Suslov) Mikhail Andreyevich Suslov (Russian: Михаи́л Андре́евич Су́слов ; 21 November [O.S. 8 November] 1902 25 January 1982) was a Soviet statesman during the Cold War.

[S002056] (HQ0048; Mikhail Suslov)  He served as Second Secretary of the Communist Party of the Soviet Union from 1965, and as unofficial Chief Ideologue of the Party until his death in 1982.

[S002057] (HQ0048; Mikhail Suslov)  Suslov was responsible for party democracy and the power separation within the Communist Party.

[S002058] (HQ0048; Mikhail Suslov)  His hardline attitude toward change made him one of the foremost anti-reformist Soviet leaders.

[S002059] (HQ0048; Ephraim Sklyansky) Ephraim Markovich Sklyansky (Russian: Эфраим Маркович Склянский ) (August 12 [O.S. July 31] 1892 - August 27, 1925) was a Soviet statesman.

[S002060] (HQ0048; Ephraim Sklyansky)  He joined the Bolsheviks during his years as a student in the medical faculty of Kiev University, from which he graduated in 1916; he was immediately drafted into the army, where he served as a doctor and became prominent in the clandestine military organizations of the Bolsheviks.

[S002061] (HQ0048; Ephraim Sklyansky)  At the time of the October Revolution he was a member of the Military Revolutionary Committee of the Petrograd Soviet; on meeting him in November, Leon Trotsky was so impressed with his "great creative "élan" combined with concentrated attention to detail" that he appointed him his deputy on the Revolutionary Military Council, where he served with distinction during the Russian Civil War (1918-1920) and helped improve the fighting condition of the Red Army—Trotsky called him the Carnot of the Russian Revolution.

[S002062] (HQ0048; Ephraim Sklyansky)  In 1924 his position as Trotsky's deputy was taken over by Grigory Zinoviev's ally Mikhail Frunze.

[S002063] (HQ0048; Ephraim Sklyansky)  Instead, he was made chairman of the Mossukno state textile trust, and the following May he left on a tour of Germany, France, and the United States to acquire technical information.

[S002064] (HQ0048; Ephraim Sklyansky)  On August 27, 1925 he died in a boating accident on Long Lake (New York) along with , the first head of Amtorg Trading Corporation.

[S002065] (HQ0048; Ephraim Sklyansky)  The high-ranking Soviet defector Boris Bazhanov was convinced that Sklyansky had been drowned on Stalin's orders, and the alleged accident had been organized by and Genrikh Yagoda.

[S002066] (HQ0048; World Summit of Nobel Peace Laureates) The World Summit of Nobel Peace Laureates was initiated by Mikhail Gorbachev in the 90s, as a forum in which the Nobel Peace Laureates and the Peace Laureate Organizations could come together to address global issues with a view to encourage and support peace and human well being in the world.

[S002067] (HQ0048; World Summit of Nobel Peace Laureates)  Its Permanent Secretariat is an independent, non-profit, ECOSOC non-governmental organization, based in Rome, operating on a permanent basis.

[S002068] (HQ0048; World Summit of Nobel Peace Laureates)  A permanent staff, mainly composed of volunteers, promotes the work of the Nobel Peace Prize Winners and organizes the World Summit of Nobel Peace Laureates on a yearly basis.

[S002069] (HQ0048; World Summit of Nobel Peace Laureates)  To date, the Permanent Secretariat has organized 16 Summits, the most recent having been held in February 2017 in the city of Bogota, Colombia.

[S002070] (HQ0048; World Summit of Nobel Peace Laureates)  This was the first time that the Summit took place in Latin America.

[S002071] (HQ0048; Anastas Mikoyan) Anastas Ivanovich Mikoyan ; 25 November 1895 – 21 October 1978) was an Old Bolshevik and Soviet statesman during the mandates of Lenin, Stalin, Khrushchev, and Brezhnev.

[S002072] (HQ0048; Anastas Mikoyan)  He was the only Soviet politician who managed to remain at the highest levels of power within the Communist Party of the Soviet Union, as that power oscillated between the Central Committee and the Politburo, from the latter days of Lenin's rule, throughout the eras of Stalin and Khrushchev, until his peaceful retirement after the first months of Brezhnev's rule.

[S002073] (HQ0048; Mikhail Gorbachev) Mikhail Sergeyevich Gorbachev, ( ; Russian: Михаи́л Серге́евич Горбачёв ; ] ; born 2 March 1931) is a former Soviet statesman.

[S002074] (HQ0048; Mikhail Gorbachev)  He was the eighth and last leader of the Soviet Union, having been General Secretary of the Communist Party of the Soviet Union from 1985 until 1991.

[S002075] (HQ0048; Mikhail Gorbachev)  He was the country's head of state from 1988 until 1991 (titled as Chairman of the Presidium of the Supreme Soviet from 1988 to 1989, as Chairman of the from 1989 to 1990, and as Soviet Union]] from 1990 to 1991).

[S002076] (HQ0048; David Waksberg) David Jonathan Waksberg, born December 14, 1956 in New York City, was a leading activist in the Soviet Jewry Movement during the 1980s and early 1990s.

[S002077] (HQ0048; David Waksberg)  In the 1970s he became involved in the Student Struggle for Soviet Jewry.

[S002078] (HQ0048; David Waksberg)  In the early 1980s he moved to California and began working for the Bay Area Council for Soviet Jews, first as Assistant Director, and later as Executive Director.

[S002079] (HQ0048; David Waksberg)  He initiated public and political activities on behalf of Soviet Jewry, supervised research and monitoring of their welfare and coordinated financial, medical and legal aid to Refuseniks and Prisoners of Conscience trapped in the Soviet Union.

[S002080] (HQ0048; David Waksberg)  He organized numerous protest demonstrations and vigils to raise public awareness of the plight of Jews in the USSR.

[S002081] (HQ0048; David Waksberg)  In 1985 Waksberg became National Vice-President of BACSJ's umbrella organization, the Union of Councils for Soviet Jews.

[S002082] (HQ0048; David Waksberg)  Waksberg frequently visited Jewish communities the Soviet Union and the Former Soviet states and coordinated briefings of the American travelers interested in visiting those communities.

[S002083] (HQ0048; David Waksberg)  In 1990 Waksberg took on the role of Director of the Center for Jewish Renewal, newly established by UCSJ.

[S002084] (HQ0048; David Waksberg)  The mission of the CJR was to promote the renewal and development of Jewish life in the USSR and the emigration rights, human rights and resettlement needs of Jews in the Former Soviet Union.

[S002085] (HQ0048; David Waksberg)  The CJR established a network of human rights and emigration bureaus in major cities of the former Soviet Union.

[S002086] (HQ0048; David Waksberg)  In mid-1990s Waksberg was a member of Bay Area Council's Board of Directors and served as Director of Development and Communication of the UCSJ.

[S002087] (HQ0048; David Waksberg)  Since 2007 Waksberg serves as Executive Director of the Bureau of Jewish Education of San Francisco.

[S002088] (HQ0048; Sergo Mikoyan) Sergo Anastasi Mikoyan (Armenian: Սերգո Անաստասի Միկոյան ; Russian: Сергo Анаста́сович Микоян ; June 5, 1929 – March 7, 2010) was one of the Soviet Union's leading historians who specialized on the foreign policies of the Soviet Union and the United States in Latin America.

[S002089] (HQ0048; Sergo Mikoyan)  He was the son of Anastas Mikoyan, an Old Bolshevik and high level Soviet statesman and adviser to Soviet leader Nikita Khrushchev.

[S002090] (HQ0049; Silene latifolia) Silene latifolia (formerly "Melandrium album"), the white campion is a dioecious flowering plant in the family Caryophyllaceae, native to most of Europe, Western Asia and Northern Africa.

[S002091] (HQ0049; Silene latifolia)  It is a herbaceous annual, occasionally biennial or a short-lived perennial plant, growing to between 40-80 centimetres tall.

[S002092] (HQ0049; Silene latifolia)  It is also known in the USA as bladder campion but should not be confused with "Silene vulgaris", which is more generally called Bladder Campion.

[S002093] (HQ0049; Silene tomentosa) Silene tomentosa, the Gibraltar campion, is a very rare flowering plant of the genus "Silene" and the family Caryophyllaceae.

[S002094] (HQ0049; Silene tomentosa)  It is a woody-based perennial about 40cm high, with bilobed flowers ranging from pink to pale violet and is endemic to Gibraltar.

[S002095] (HQ0049; Silene conoidea) Silene conoidea is a species of flowering plant in the pink family known by the common names weed silene and large sand catchfly.

[S002096] (HQ0049; Silene conoidea)  It is native to Eurasia, and it is known in other parts of the world, such as western North America, as a weed.

[S002097] (HQ0049; Silene conoidea)  It is an annual herb growing up to a meter in height with a hairy, partially glandular stem.

[S002098] (HQ0049; Silene conoidea)  The lance-shaped leaves are up to 12 centimeters long near the base of the plant and smaller farther up.

[S002099] (HQ0049; Silene conoidea)  The flower is enclosed in an inflated, hairy, glandular calyx of fused sepals which is ridged with many veins.

[S002100] (HQ0049; Silene conoidea)  It is open at the top, revealing five bright pink petals.

[S002101] (HQ0049; Silene) Silene is a genus of flowering plants in the family Caryophyllaceae.

[S002102] (HQ0049; Silene)  Containing approximately 700 species, it is the largest genus in the family.

[S002103] (HQ0049; Silene)  Common names include campion (which is shared with the related genus "Lychnis") and catchfly.

[S002104] (HQ0049; Silene)  Many "Silene" species are widely distributed, particularly in the northern hemisphere.

[S002105] (HQ0049; Silene stenophylla) Silene stenophylla is a species of flowering plant in the family Caryophyllaceae.

[S002106] (HQ0049; Silene stenophylla)  Commonly called narrow-leafed campion, it is a species in the genus "Silene".

[S002107] (HQ0049; Silene stenophylla)  It grows in the Arctic tundra of far eastern Siberia and the mountains of Northern Japan.

[S002108] (HQ0049; Silene stenophylla)  Frozen samples, estimated via radiocarbon dating to be around 32,000 years old, were discovered in the same area as current living specimens, and in 2012 a team of scientists successfully regenerated a plant from the samples.

[S002109] (HQ0049; Silene menziesii) Silene menziesii is a species of flowering plant in the pink family known by the common names Menzies' campion and Menzies' catchfly.

[S002110] (HQ0049; Silene menziesii)  It is native to western North America from Alaska through the western half of Canada to the southwestern United States.

[S002111] (HQ0049; Silene menziesii)  It can be found in many types of habitat and it is quite common in much of its range.

[S002112] (HQ0049; Silene menziesii)  It is variable in morphology and there are a number of varied subtaxa.

[S002113] (HQ0049; Silene menziesii)  In general, it is a perennial herb growing from a caudex, appearing matlike, decumbent, or erect, with stems a few centimeters to over half a meter long.

[S002114] (HQ0049; Silene menziesii)  It is usually hairy in texture, with upper parts bearing sticky glandular hairs.

[S002115] (HQ0049; Silene menziesii)  The leaves are lance-shaped, oppositely arranged in pairs, and a few centimeters in length, upper leaves usually smaller than lower.

[S002116] (HQ0049; Silene menziesii)  Flowers may occur in a cyme at the top of the stem, or in leaf axils, or both.

[S002117] (HQ0049; Silene menziesii)  Each is encapsulated in a hairy, veined calyx of fused sepals.

[S002118] (HQ0049; Silene menziesii)  The petals are white with two lobes at the tips.

[S002119] (HQ0049; Silene menziesii)  The plant is dioecious with male and female plants producing different flowers.

[S002120] (HQ0049; Silene menziesii)  The male and female flower types look the same externally; the stamens are reduced in female plants and the stigmas are reduced in the male.

[S002121] (HQ0049; Silene suksdorfii) Silene suksdorfii is a species of flowering plant in the pink family known by the common names Suksdorf's silene, Suksdorf's catchfly and Cascade alpine campion.

[S002122] (HQ0049; Silene suksdorfii)  It is native to the Pacific Northwest of the United States, where it occurs from Washington and Idaho to northern California.

[S002123] (HQ0049; Silene suksdorfii)  It is mainly an alpine species, growing in the talus of high mountain slopes.

[S002124] (HQ0049; Silene suksdorfii)  It can also be found below the tree line in forested subalpine habitat.

[S002125] (HQ0049; Silene suksdorfii)  It is a squat perennial herb producing several erect stems from a leafy, woody caudex.

[S002126] (HQ0049; Silene suksdorfii)  It generally takes a clumpy form.

[S002127] (HQ0049; Silene suksdorfii)  The stems grow up to 10 or 15 centimeters tall and are hairy in texture, with glandular, sticky areas on the upper parts.

[S002128] (HQ0049; Silene suksdorfii)  The leaves occur in tufts around the caudex.

[S002129] (HQ0049; Silene suksdorfii)  They are fleshy and coated in soft hairs.

[S002130] (HQ0049; Silene suksdorfii)  Solitary flowers arise on erect peduncles.

[S002131] (HQ0049; Silene suksdorfii)  Each is encapsulated in an inflated calyx of fused sepals, which is starkly purple-veined and has purplish glandular hairs.

[S002132] (HQ0049; Silene suksdorfii)  The petals are white or purple-tinged and have two lobes at their tips and appendages at their bases.

[S002133] (HQ0049; Ferocactus) Ferocactus is a genus of large barrel-shaped cacti, mostly with large spines and small flowers.

[S002134] (HQ0049; Ferocactus)  There are about 30 species included in the genus.

[S002135] (HQ0049; Ferocactus)  They are found in the southwestern United States and northwestern Mexico.

[S002136] (HQ0049; Silene antirrhina) Silene antirrhina is a species of flowering plant in the pink family known by the common names sleepy silene and sleepy catchfly.

[S002137] (HQ0049; Silene antirrhina)  It is native to the Americas, where it is widespread throughout North America and parts of South America.

[S002138] (HQ0049; Silene antirrhina)  It is known in Europe as an introduced species.

[S002139] (HQ0049; Sex determination in Silene) "Silene" are a flowering plant that evolved a dioecious reproductive system.

[S002140] (HQ0049; Sex determination in Silene)  This is made possible through heteromorphic sex chromosomes expressed as XY.

[S002141] (HQ0049; Sex determination in Silene)  "Silene" recently evolved sex chromosomes 5-10 million years ago and are widely used by geneticists and biologists to study the mechanisms of sex determination since they are one of only 39 species across 14 families of angiosperm that possess sex-determining genes.

[S002142] (HQ0049; Sex determination in Silene)  "Silene" are studied because of their ability to produce offspring with a plethora of reproductive systems.

[S002143] (HQ0049; Sex determination in Silene)  The common inference drawn from such studies is that the sex of the offspring is determined by the Y chromosome.

[S002144] (HQ0050; No. 2 Squadron RAAF) No. 2 Squadron is a Royal Australian Air Force (RAAF) squadron that operates from RAAF Base Williamtown, near Newcastle, New South Wales.

[S002145] (HQ0050; No. 2 Squadron RAAF)  From its formation in 1916 as part of the Australian Flying Corps, it has flown a variety of aircraft types including fighters, bombers, and Airborne Early Warning & Control (AEW&C).

[S002146] (HQ0050; No. 2 Squadron RAAF)  During World War I, the squadron operated on the Western Front conducting fighter sweeps and ground-attack missions.

[S002147] (HQ0050; No. 2 Squadron RAAF)  It was disbanded in mid-1919, following the end of hostilities.

[S002148] (HQ0050; No. 2 Squadron RAAF)  The squadron was briefly re-raised in 1922 as part of the newly independent RAAF, but was disbanded after only a couple of months and not reformed until 1937.

[S002149] (HQ0050; No. 2 Squadron RAAF)  It saw action as a bomber unit in the South West Pacific theatre of World War II and, equipped with English Electric Canberra jets, in the Malayan Emergency and the Vietnam War.

[S002150] (HQ0050; No. 2 Squadron RAAF)  The squadron was again disbanded in 1982, following the retirement of the Canberra.

[S002151] (HQ0050; No. 2 Squadron RAAF)  It was re-formed in 2000 to operate the Boeing 737 AEW&C "Wedgetail".

[S002152] (HQ0050; No. 2 Squadron RAAF)  One of the six Boeing 737s was deployed to the Middle East in September 2014, as part of Australia's contribution to the military coalition against ISIS.

[S002153] (HQ0050; South West Pacific theatre of World War II) The South West Pacific theatre, during World War II, was a major theatre of the war between the Allies and Japan.

[S002154] (HQ0050; South West Pacific theatre of World War II)  It included the Philippines, the Dutch East Indies (except for Sumatra), Borneo, Australia and its mandate Territory of New Guinea (including the Bismarck Archipelago) and the western part of the Solomon Islands.

[S002155] (HQ0050; South West Pacific theatre of World War II)  This area was defined by the Allied powers' South West Pacific Area (SWPA) command.

[S002156] (HQ0050; English Electric Canberra) The English Electric Canberra is a British first-generation jet-powered medium bomber that was manufactured during the 1950s.

[S002157] (HQ0050; English Electric Canberra)  It was developed by English Electric during the mid-to-late 1940s in response to a 1944 Air Ministry requirement for a successor to the wartime de Havilland Mosquito fast-bomber.

[S002158] (HQ0050; English Electric Canberra)  Amongst the performance requirements for the type was the demand for an outstanding high altitude bombing capability in addition to flying at high speeds.

[S002159] (HQ0050; English Electric Canberra)  These were partly accomplished by making use of newly developed jet propulsion technology.

[S002160] (HQ0050; English Electric Canberra)  When the Canberra was introduced to service with the Royal Air Force (RAF), the type's first operator, in May 1951, it became the service's first jet-powered bomber aircraft.

[S002161] (HQ0050; Asiatic-Pacific Theater) The Asiatic-Pacific Theater, was the theater of operations of U.S. forces during World War II in the Pacific War during 1941-45.

[S002162] (HQ0050; Asiatic-Pacific Theater)  From mid-1942 until the end of the war in 1945, there were two U.S. operational commands in the Pacific.

[S002163] (HQ0050; Asiatic-Pacific Theater)  The Pacific Ocean Areas (POA), divided into the Central Pacific Area, the North Pacific Area and the South Pacific Area, were commanded by Admiral Chester W. Nimitz, Commander-in-Chief Pacific Ocean Areas.

[S002164] (HQ0050; Asiatic-Pacific Theater)  The South West Pacific Area (SWPA) was commanded by General Douglas MacArthur, Supreme Allied Commander South West Pacific Area.

[S002165] (HQ0050; Asiatic-Pacific Theater)  During 1945, the United States added the United States Strategic Air Forces in the Pacific, commanded by General Carl A. Spaatz.

[S002166] (HQ0050; Savoia-Marchetti SM.79) The Savoia-Marchetti SM.79 "Sparviero" (Italian for sparrowhawk) was a three-engined Italian medium bomber with a wood-and-metal structure.

[S002167] (HQ0050; Savoia-Marchetti SM.79)  Originally designed as a fast passenger aircraft, between 1937 and 1939 this low-wing monoplane set 26 world records, qualifying it for some time as the fastest medium bomber in the world.

[S002168] (HQ0050; Savoia-Marchetti SM.79)  It first saw action during the Spanish Civil War and flew on all fronts in which Italy was involved during World War II.

[S002169] (HQ0050; Savoia-Marchetti SM.79)  It achieved success as a torpedo bomber in the Mediterranean theater, and became the best-known Italian aeroplane of the war.

[S002170] (HQ0050; Savoia-Marchetti SM.79)  It was easily recognizable due to its distinctive fuselage dorsal "hump", and was well liked by its crews, who nicknamed it "il gobbo maledetto" ("damned hunchback").

[S002171] (HQ0050; South West Pacific Area (command)) South West Pacific Area (SWPA) was the name given to the Allied supreme military command in the South West Pacific Theatre of World War II.

[S002172] (HQ0050; South West Pacific Area (command))  It was one of four major Allied commands in the Pacific War.

[S002173] (HQ0050; South West Pacific Area (command))  SWPA included the Philippines, Borneo, the Dutch East Indies (excluding Sumatra), East Timor, Australia, the Territories of Papua and New Guinea, and the western part of the Solomon Islands.

[S002174] (HQ0050; South West Pacific Area (command))  It primarily consisted of United States and Australian forces, although Dutch, Filipino, British and other Allied forces also served in the SWPA.

[S002175] (HQ0050; Tupolev Tu-12) The Tupolev Tu-12 (development designation Tu-77) was an experimental Soviet jet-powered medium bomber developed from the successful piston-engined Tupolev Tu-2 bomber after the end of World War II.

[S002176] (HQ0050; Tupolev Tu-12)  It was designed as a transitional aircraft to familiarize Tupolev and the VVS with the issues involved with jet-engined bombers.

[S002177] (HQ0050; No. 12 Squadron RAAF) No. 12 Squadron was a Royal Australian Air Force (RAAF) general purpose, bomber and transport squadron.

[S002178] (HQ0050; No. 12 Squadron RAAF)  The squadron was formed in 1939 and saw combat in the South West Pacific theatre of World War II.

[S002179] (HQ0050; No. 12 Squadron RAAF)  From 1941 to 1943, it mainly conducted maritime patrols off northern Australia.

[S002180] (HQ0050; No. 12 Squadron RAAF)  The squadron was based at Merauke in western New Guinea from November 1943 to July 1944, when it was withdrawn from operations.

[S002181] (HQ0050; No. 12 Squadron RAAF)  After being re-equipped, it operated as a heavy bomber unit from February 1945 until the end of the war.

[S002182] (HQ0050; No. 12 Squadron RAAF)  The squadron continued in this role until it was redesignated No. 1 Squadron RAAF in February 1948.

[S002183] (HQ0050; No. 12 Squadron RAAF)  The squadron was reformed in 1973 to operate transport helicopters but was again disbanded in 1989.

[S002184] (HQ0050; Coastwatchers) The Coastwatchers, also known as the Coast Watch Organisation, Combined Field Intelligence Service or Section C, Allied Intelligence Bureau, were Allied military intelligence operatives stationed on remote Pacific islands during World War II to observe enemy movements and rescue stranded Allied personnel.

[S002185] (HQ0050; Coastwatchers)  They played a significant role in the Pacific Ocean theatre and South West Pacific theatre, particularly as an early warning network during the Guadalcanal campaign.

[S002186] (HQ0050; Edwin A. Doss) Edwin A. Doss (September 14, 1914January 7, 1996) was an American fighter pilot and commander in the U.S. Air Force during World War II and Korean War.

[S002187] (HQ0050; Edwin A. Doss)  Logging more than 4,500 flying hours, Doss flew 573 combat hours and accrued 280 combat missions during his leadership in the South West Pacific Theatre and Korean War.

[S002188] (HQ0050; Edwin A. Doss)  For his two-year service as commander of the 35th Fighter Group during World War II, Doss was awarded the Distinguished Flying Cross, Legion of Merit, and the Air Medal.

[S002189] (HQ0050; Edwin A. Doss)  He received his second Legion of Merit and the Korean Ulchi medal with a Silver Star for his assignments as commander of the 49th Fighter Bomber Wing and the 3rd Bomber Wing at Kunsan, Korea.

[S002190] (HQ0050; Edwin A. Doss)  Colonel Doss’s service has been cited as integral to the development of long-range fighter tactics in the South West Pacific Theater.
